```
<file>
00001| ;;; denote.el --- Simple notes with an efficient file-naming scheme -*- lexical-binding: t -*-
00002| 
00003| ;; Copyright (C) 2022-2025  Free Software Foundation, Inc.
00004| 
00005| ;; Author: Protesilaos Stavrou <info@protesilaos.com>
00006| ;; Maintainer: Protesilaos Stavrou <info@protesilaos.com>
00007| ;; URL: https://github.com/protesilaos/denote
00008| ;; Version: 4.1.3
00009| ;; Package-Requires: ((emacs "28.1"))
00010| 
00011| ;; This file is NOT part of GNU Emacs.
00012| 
00013| ;; This program is free software; you can redistribute it and/or modify
00014| ;; it under the terms of the GNU General Public License as published by
00015| ;; the Free Software Foundation, either version 3 of the License, or
00016| ;; (at your option) any later version.
00017| ;;
00018| ;; This program is distributed in the hope that it will be useful,
00019| ;; but WITHOUT ANY WARRANTY; without even the implied warranty of
00020| ;; MERCHANTABILITY or FITNESS FOR A PARTICULAR PURPOSE.  See the
00021| ;; GNU General Public License for more details.
00022| ;;
00023| ;; You should have received a copy of the GNU General Public License
00024| ;; along with this program.  If not, see <https://www.gnu.org/licenses/>.
00025| 
00026| ;;; Commentary:
00027| 
00028| ;; Denote is a simple note-taking tool for Emacs.  It is based on the idea
00029| ;; that notes should follow a predictable and descriptive file-naming
00030| ;; scheme.  The file name must offer a clear indication of what the note is
00031| ;; about, without reference to any other metadata.  Denote basically
00032| ;; streamlines the creation of such files while providing facilities to
00033| ;; link between them.
00034| ;;
00035| ;; Denote's file-naming scheme is not limited to "notes".  It can be used
00036| ;; for all types of file, including those that are not editable in Emacs,
00037| ;; such as videos.  Naming files in a consistent way makes their
00038| ;; filtering and retrieval considerably easier.  Denote provides relevant
00039| ;; facilities to rename files, regardless of file type.
00040| 
00041| ;;; Code:
00042| 
00043| (require 'seq)
00044| (require 'xref)
00045| (require 'dired)
00046| (eval-when-compile (require 'subr-x))
00047| 
00048| (defgroup denote ()
00049|   "Simple notes with an efficient file-naming scheme."
00050|   :group 'files

(File has more lines. Use 'offset' parameter to read beyond line 50)
</file>
```

```
00026| ;;; Commentary:
00027| 
00028| ;; Denote is a simple note-taking tool for Emacs.  It is based on the idea
00029| ;; that notes should follow a predictable and descriptive file-naming
00030| ;; scheme.  The file name must offer a clear indication of what the note is
00031| ;; about, without reference to any other metadata.  Denote basically
00032| ;; streamlines the creation of such files while providing facilities to
00033| ;; link between them.
00034| ;;
00035| ;; Denote's file-naming scheme is not limited to "notes".  It can be used
00036| ;; for all types of file, including those that are not editable in Emacs,
00037| ;; such as videos.  Naming files in a consistent way makes their
00038| ;; filtering and retrieval considerably easier.  Denote provides relevant
00039| ;; facilities to rename files, regardless of file type.
00040| 
00041| ;;; Code:
00042| 
00043| (require 'seq)
00044| (require 'xref)
00045| (require 'dired)
00046| (eval-when-compile (require 'subr-x))
00047| 
00048| (defgroup denote ()
00049|   "Simple notes with an efficient file-naming scheme."
00050|   :group 'files
00051|   :link '(info-link "(denote) Top")
00052|   :link '(url-link :tag "Homepage" "https://protesilaos.com/emacs/denote"))
00053| 
00054| ;;;; User options

00056| ;; About the autoload: (info "(elisp) File Local Variables")

00059| (defcustom denote-directory (expand-file-name "~/Documents/notes/")
00060|   "Directory, as a string, for storing personal notes.
00061| This is the destination `denote' and all other file-creating Denote
00062| commands use.
00063| 
00064| The value can also be a list of directories as strings.  In that case,
00065| `denote' and related commands will pick the first one among them, unless
00066| the user option `denote-prompts' is configured to prompt for a
00067| directory, among other possible prompts.  Files within those directories
00068| can link to each other, as they are considered part of one expansive
00069| Denote directory.
00070| 
00071| Whether the value is a string or a list of strings, all relevant Denote
00072| commands work with the subdirectories of those directories as well.  In
00073| other words, a list value is not needed to enumerate all the
00074| subdirectories of a common parent directory: simply specify the parent.
00075| 
00076| To create a \"silo\", i.e. a self-contained Denote directory whose
00077| files do no link to any file outside of it, set the value of this user
00078| option in a .dir-locals file.  Read Info node `(denote) Maintain
00079| separate directory silos for notes'.
00080| 
00081| If the target directory does not exist, `denote' and related commands
00082| will create it.
00083| 
00084| The value of this variable is read by commands other than `denote', such
00085| as `denote-link', `denote-backlinks', `denote-dired', and `denote-grep',
00086| among others.  File-renaming commands such as `denote-rename-file' and
00087| `denote-dired-rename-marked-files' can still be used on any file
00088| anywhere on the file system.
00089| 
00090| To use the value of this variable from Lisp, call the function
00091| `denote-directories'."
00092|   :group 'denote
00093|   :safe (lambda (val) (or (stringp val) (listp val) (eq val 'local) (eq val 'default-directory)))
00094|   :package-version '(denote . "4.1.0")
00095|   :link '(info-link "(denote) Maintain separate directories for notes")
00096|   :type '(choice (directory :tag "Single directory")
00097|                  (repeat :tag "List of directories" directory)))

00101| (defcustom denote-save-buffers nil
00102|   "Control whether to save buffers automatically.
00103| This applies to commands that create new notes, such as `denote', or
00104| those that rename existing files, such as `denote-rename-file'.
00105| 
00106| By default (a nil value), Denote does not save such buffers, giving
00107| users the chance to review the text before writing it to the file.
00108|

00110| modifies.

00117| (defcustom denote-kill-buffers nil
00118|   "Control whether creation or renaming commands kill their buffer.
00119| 
00120| The default behaviour of creation or renaming commands such as
00121| `denote' or `denote-rename-file' is to not kill the buffer they
00122| create or modify at the end of their operation.
00123| 
00124| If this user option is nil (the default), buffers affected by a
00125| creation or renaming command are not automatically killed.
00126| 
00127| If set to `on-creation', new notes are automatically killed.
00128| 
00129| If set to `on-rename', renamed notes are automatically killed.
00130| 
00131| If set to t, new and renamed notes are killed.
00132| 
00133| If a buffer is killed, it is also saved, as if `denote-save-buffers'
00134| were t. See its documentation.
00135| 
00136| In all cases, if the buffer already existed before the Denote operation
00137| it is NOT automatically killed."
00138|   :group 'denote
00139|   :package-version '(denote . "3.1.0")
00140|   :type '(choice
00141|           (const :tag "Do not kill buffers" nil)
00142|           (const :tag "Kill after creation" on-creation)
00143|           (const :tag "Kill after rename" on-rename)
00144|           (const :tag "Kill after creation and rename" t)))

00147| (defcustom denote-known-keywords
00148|   '("emacs" "philosophy" "politics" "economics")
00149|   "List of strings with predefined keywords.
00150| This is used by the `denote-keywords-prompt' to get keywords when
00151| creating or renaming a file, such as via the commands `denote' and
00152| `denote-rename-file'.
00153| 
00154| The `denote-keywords-prompt' does not enforce the keywords defined in
00155| `denote-known-keywords', as users can input arbitrary text.  Those newly
00156| introduced keywords are then available for completion, if
00157| `denote-infer-keywords' is set to a non-nil value (its default).  If
00158| `denote-infer-keywords' is nil, then the `denote-keywords-prompt' only
00159| accepts input that is among the `denote-known-keywords'.
00160|

00167| ;;;###autoload (put 'denote-infer-keywords 'safe-local-variable (lambda (val) (or val (null val))))
00168| (defcustom denote-infer-keywords t
00169|   "Whether to infer keywords from existing notes' file names.
00170| 
00171| When non-nil (the default), search the file names of existing notes in
00172| the variable `denote-directory' for their keyword field and extract the
00173| entries as \"inferred keywords\".  These are combined with
00174| `denote-known-keywords' and are presented as completion candidates while
00175| using `denote' and related commands interactively.
00176| 
00177| If nil, refrain from inferring keywords.  In this case, make the
00178| aforementioned completion prompt show just the `denote-known-keywords'
00179| and enforce them as the only acceptable input.  Use this if you want to
00180| work with a controlled vocabulary.
00181|

00183| exclude keywords that match a regular expression.
00184| 
00185| Inferred keywords are specific to the value of the variable
00186| `denote-directory'.  In a silo, as explained in that variable's doc
00187| string, the inferred keywords are specific to the silo."

00189|   :safe (lambda (val) (or val (null val)))
00190|   :package-version '(denote . "4.2.0")
00191|   :type 'boolean)
00192| 
00193| (defcustom denote-prompts '(title keywords)
00194|   "Specify the prompts followed by relevant Denote commands.
00195| 
00196| Commands that prompt for user input to construct a Denote file name
00197| include, but are not limited to: `denote', `denote-signature',
00198| `denote-type', `denote-date', `denote-subdirectory',
00199| `denote-rename-file', `denote-dired-rename-files'.
00200| 
00201| The value of this user option is a list of symbols, which includes any
00202| of the following:
00203| 
00204| - `title': Prompt for the title of the new note.
00205| 
00206| - `keywords': Prompts with completion for the keywords of the new note.
00207|   Available candidates are those specified in the user option
00208|   `denote-known-keywords'.  If the user option `denote-infer-keywords'
00209|   is non-nil, keywords in existing note file names are included in the
00210|   list of candidates.  The `keywords' prompt uses `completing-read-multiple',
00211|   meaning that it can accept multiple keywords separated by a comma (or
00212|   whatever the value of `crm-separator' is).
00213| 
00214| - `file-type': Prompts with completion for the file type of the new
00215|   note.  Available candidates are those specified in the user option
00216|   `denote-file-type'.  Without this prompt, `denote' uses the value of
00217|   the variable `denote-file-type'.
00218| 
00219| - `subdirectory': Prompts with completion for a subdirectory in which to
00220|   create the note.  Available candidates are the value of the user
00221|   option `denote-directory' and all of its subdirectories.  Any
00222|   subdirectory must already exist: Denote will not create it.
00223| 
00224| - `date': Prompts for the date of the new note.  It will expect an input
00225|   like 2022-06-16 or a date plus time: 2022-06-16 14:30.  Without the
00226|   `date' prompt, the `denote' command uses the `current-time'.  (To
00227|   leverage the more sophisticated Org method, see the
00228|   `denote-date-prompt-use-org-read-date'.)
00229| 
00230| - `identifier': Prompts for the identifier of the new note.  It expects
00231|   a string that has the format of `denote-date-identifier-format'.
00232| 
00233| - `template': Prompts for a KEY among `denote-templates'.  The value of
00234|   that KEY is used to populate the new note with content, which is added
00235|   after the front matter.
00236| 
00237| - `signature': Prompts for an arbitrary string that can be used for any
00238|   kind of workflow, such as a special tag to label the part1 and part2
00239|   of a large file that is split in half, or to add special contexts like
00240|   home and work, or even priorities like a, b, c. One other use-case is
00241|   to implement a sequencing scheme that makes notes have hierarchical
00242|   relationships.  This is handled by our optional extension
00243|   denote-sequence.el, which is part of the denote package (read the
00244|   manual).
00245| 
00246| The prompts occur in the given order.
00247| 
00248| If the value of this user option is nil, no prompts are used.  The
00249| resulting file name will consist of an identifier (i.e. the date and
00250| time) and a supported file type extension (per the variable
00251| `denote-file-type').
00252| 
00253| Recall that Denote's standard file-naming scheme is defined as
00254| follows (read the manual for the technicalities):
00255| 
00256|     ID--TITLE__KEYWORDS.EXT
00257| 
00258| Depending on the inclusion of the `title', `keywords', and
00259| `signature' prompts, file names will be any of those
00260| permutations:
00261| 
00262|     ID.EXT
00263|     ID--TITLE.EXT
00264|     ID__KEYWORDS.EXT
00265|     ID==SIGNATURE.EXT
00266|     ID==SIGNATURE--TITLE.EXT
00267|     ID==SIGNATURE--TITLE__KEYWORDS.EXT
00268|     ID==SIGNATURE__KEYWORDS.EXT
00269| 
00270| When in doubt, always include the `title' and `keywords'
00271| prompts (the default style).
00272| 
00273| Finally, this user option only affects the interactive use of the
00274| `denote' or other relevant commands (advanced users can call it from
00275| Lisp).  In Lisp usage, the behaviour is always what the caller
00276| specifies, based on the supplied arguments.
00277| 
00278| Also see `denote-history-completion-in-prompts'.
00279| 
00280| To change the order of the file name components, refer to
00281| `denote-file-name-components-order'."
00282|   :group 'denote
00283|   :package-version '(denote . "2.3.0")
00284|   :link '(info-link "(denote) The denote-prompts option")
00285|   :type '(radio (const :tag "Use no prompts" nil)
00286|                 (set :tag "Available prompts" :greedy t
00287|                      (const :tag "Title" title)
00288|                      (const :tag "Keywords" keywords)
00289|                      (const :tag "Date" date)
00290|                      (const :tag "Identifier" identifier)
00291|                      (const :tag "File type extension" file-type)
00292|                      (const :tag "Subdirectory" subdirectory)
00293|                      (const :tag "Template" template)
00294|                      (const :tag "Signature" signature))))
00295| 
00296| (defcustom denote-file-name-components-order '(identifier signature title keywords)
00297|   "Specify the order of the file name components.
00298| 
00299| The value is a list of the following symbols:
00300| 
00301| - `identifier': This is the combination of the date and time.  When it
00302|   is the first on the list, it looks like \"20240519T073456\" and does
00303|   not have a component separator of its own due its unambiguous format.
00304|   When it is placed anywhere else in the file name, it is prefixed with
00305|   \"@@\", so it looks like \"@@20240519T073456\".
00306| 
00307| - `signature': This is an arbitrary string that can be used to qualify
00308|   the file in some way, according to the user's methodology (e.g. to add
00309|   a sequence to notes).  The string is always prefixed with the \"==\"
00310|   to remain unambiguous.
00311| 
00312| - `title': This is an arbitrary string which describes the file.  It is
00313|   always prefixed with \"--\" to be unambiguous.
00314| 
00315| - `keywords': This is a series of one or more words that succinctly
00316|   group the file.  Multiple keywords are separated by an underscore
00317|   prefixed to each of them.  The file name component is always prefixed
00318|   with \"__\".
00319| 
00320| All four symbols must appear exactly once.  Duplicates are ignored.  Any
00321| missing symbol is added automatically.
00322| 
00323| Some examples:
00324| 
00325|     (setq denote-file-name-components-order
00326|        \\='(identifier signature title keywords))
00327|     => 20240519T07345==hello--this-is-the-title__denote_testing.org
00328| 
00329|     (setq denote-file-name-components-order
00330|        \\='(signature identifier title keywords))
00331|     => ==hello@@20240519T07345--this-is-the-title__denote_testing.org
00332| 
00333|     (setq denote-file-name-components-order
00334|        \\='(title signature identifier keywords))
00335|     => --this-is-the-title==hello@@20240519T07345__denote_testing.org
00336| 
00337|     (setq denote-file-name-components-order
00338|        \\='(keywords title signature identifier))
00339|     => __denote_testing--this-is-the-title==hello@@20240519T07345.org
00340| 
00341| Also see the user option `denote-prompts', which affects which
00342| components are actually used in the order specified herein.
00343| 
00344| Before deciding on this, please consider the longer-term implications
00345| of file names with varying patterns. Consistency makes things
00346| predictable and thus easier to find. So pick one order and never touch
00347| it again. When in doubt, leave the default file-naming scheme as-is.
00348| 
00349| This user option should only be used to build a file name.  Custom code
00350| should not have behaviors that depend on its value.  The reason is that
00351| its value can change over time and Denote should be able to handle past
00352| and current notes."
00353|   :group 'denote
00354|   :package-version '(denote . "3.0.0")
00355|   ;; FIXME 2024-05-19: This technically works to display the user
00356|   ;; option in the Custom buffer and to show its current value, though
00357|   ;; it does not allow the user to modify it graphically: they have to
00358|   ;; switch to the Lisp expression.  Find a way to present an
00359|   ;; interface that lets the user reorder those elements.
00360|   ;;
00361|   ;; Still, making this a defcustom helps with discoverability, as
00362|   ;; well as with the use of `setopt' and related.
00363|   :type '(list
00364|           (const :tag "Identifier component (date and time)" identifier)
00365|           (const :tag "File signature (text to qualify a file)" signature)
00366|           (const :tag "The title of the file" title)
00367|           (const :tag "Keywords of the file" keywords)))
00368| 
00369| (defcustom denote-front-matter-components-present-even-if-empty-value '(title keywords date identifier)

00404| (defcustom denote-file-type nil
00405|   "The file type extension for new notes.
00406| 
00407| By default (a nil value), the file type is that of Org mode.
00408| Though the `org' symbol can be specified for the same effect.
00409| 
00410| When the value is the symbol `markdown-yaml', the file type is
00411| that of Markdown mode and the front matter uses YAML notation.
00412| Similarly, `markdown-toml' is Markdown but has TOML syntax in the
00413| front matter.
00414| 
00415| When the value is `text', the file type is that of Text mode.
00416| 
00417| Any other non-nil value is the same as the default.
00418| 
00419| NOTE: Expert users can change the supported file-types by editing
00420| the value of `denote-file-types'.  That variable, which is not a
00421| user option, controls the behaviour of all file-type-aware
00422| functions (creating notes, renaming them, inserting front matter,
00423| formatting a link, etc.). Consult its documentation for the
00424| technicalities."
00425|   :type '(choice

00428|           (const :tag "Markdown (YAML front matter)" markdown-yaml)
00429|           (const :tag "Markdown (TOML front matter)" markdown-toml)
00430|           (const :tag "Plain text" text))

00433| 
00434| (defcustom denote-date-format nil
00435|   "Date format in the front matter (file header) of new notes.
00436| 
00437| When nil (the default value), use a file-type-specific
00438| format (also check the user option `denote-file-type'):
00439| 
00440| - For Org, an inactive timestamp is used, such as [2022-06-30 Wed
00441|   15:31].
00442| 
00443| - For Markdown, the RFC3339 standard is applied:
00444|   2022-06-30T15:48:00+03:00.
00445| 
00446| - For plain text, the format is that of ISO 8601: 2022-06-30.
00447| 
00448| If the value is a string, ignore the above and use it instead.
00449| The string must include format specifiers for the date.  These
00450| are described in the doc string of `format-time-string'."

00452|           (const :tag "Use appropiate format for each file type" nil)

00457| (defcustom denote-date-prompt-use-org-read-date nil

00459| 
00460| If non-nil, use `org-read-date'.  If nil, input the date as a
00461| string, as described in `denote'.
00462| 
00463| This option is relevant when `denote-prompts' includes a `date'
00464| and/or when the user invokes the command `denote-date'."
00465|   :group 'denote
00466|   :package-version '(denote . "0.6.0")
00467|   :type 'boolean)
00468| 
00469| (defcustom denote-org-store-link-to-heading nil
00470|   "Determine whether `org-store-link' links to the current Org heading.
00471| 
00472| [ Remember that what `org-store-link' does is merely collect a link.  To
00473|   actually insert it, use the command `org-insert-link'.  Note that
00474|   `org-capture' uses `org-store-link' internally when it needs to store
00475|   a link.  ]
00476| 
00477| When the value is nil, the Denote handler for `org-store-link' produces
00478| links only to the current file (by using the file's identifier).  For
00479| example:
00480| 
00481|     [[denote:20240118T060608][Some test]]
00482| 
00483| If the value is `context', the link consists of the file's identifier
00484| and the text of the current heading, like this:
00485| 
00486|     [[denote:20240118T060608::*Heading text][Some test::Heading text]].
00487| 
00488| However, if there already exists a CUSTOM_ID property for the current
00489| heading, this is always given priority and is used instead of the
00490| context.
00491| 
00492| If the value is `id' or, for backward-compatibility, any other non-nil
00493| value, then Denote will use the standard Org mechanism of the CUSTOM_ID
00494| property to create a unique link to the heading.  If the heading does
00495| not have a CUSTOM_ID, it creates it and includes it in its PROPERTIES
00496| drawer.  If a CUSTOM_ID exists, it takes it as-is.  The result is like
00497| this:
00498| 
00499|     [[denote:20240118T060608::#h:eed0fb8e-4cc7-478f][Some test::Heading text]]
00500| 
00501| The value of the CUSTOM_ID is determined by the Org user option
00502| `org-id-method'.  The sample shown above uses the default UUID
00503| infrastructure (though I deleted a few characters to not get
00504| complaints from the byte compiler about long lines in the doc
00505| string...).
00506| 
00507| Note that this option does not affect how Org behaves with regard to
00508| `org-id-link-to-org-use-id'.  If that user option is set to create ID
00509| properties, then those will be created by Org even if the Denote link
00510| handler will take care to not use/store the ID value.  Concretely, users
00511| who never want ID properties under their headings should keep
00512| `org-id-link-to-org-use-id' in its nil value.
00513| 
00514| Context links are easier to break than those with a CUSTOM_ID in cases
00515| where either the heading text changes or there is another heading that
00516| matches that text.  The potential advantage of context links is that
00517| they do not require a PROPERTIES drawer.
00518| 
00519| When visiting a link to a heading, Org opens the Denote file and then
00520| navigates to that heading.
00521| 
00522| [ This feature only works in Org mode files, as other file types
00523|   do not have a linking mechanism that handles unique identifiers
00524|   for headings or other patterns to jump to.  If `org-store-link'
00525|   is invoked in one such file, it captures only the Denote
00526|   identifier of the file, even if this user option is set to a
00527|   non-nil value.  ]"
00528|   :group 'denote
00529|   :package-version '(denote . "4.0.0")
00530|   :type '(choice (const :tag "No link to heading (default)" nil)
00531|                  (const :tag "Link to the context" context)
00532|                  (const :tag "Link wtih CUSTOM_ID, creating it if needed" id)))
00533| 
00534| (defcustom denote-templates nil
00535|   "Alist of content templates for new notes.
00536| A template is arbitrary text that Denote will add to a newly
00537| created note right below the front matter.
00538| 
00539| Templates are expressed as a (KEY . VALUE) association.
00540| 
00541| - The KEY is the name which identifies the template.  It is an
00542|   arbitrary symbol, such as `report', `memo', `statement'.
00543| 
00544| - The VALUE is either a string or the symbol of a function.
00545| 
00546|   - If it is a string, it is ordinary text that Denote will insert
00547|     as-is.  It can contain newline characters to add spacing.  The
00548|     manual of Denote contains examples on how to use the `concat'
00549|     function, beside writing a generic string.
00550| 
00551|   - If it is a function, it is called without arguments and is expected
00552|     to return a string.  Denote will call the function and insert the
00553|     result in the buffer.
00554| 
00555| The user can choose a template either by invoking the command
00556| `denote-template' or by changing the user option `denote-prompts'
00557| to always prompt for a template when calling the `denote'
00558| command."
00559|   :type '(alist :key-type symbol :value-type (choice string function))
00560|   :package-version '(denote . "3.1.0")
00561|   :link '(info-link "(denote) The denote-templates option")
00562|   :group 'denote)
00563| 
00564| (defcustom denote-rename-confirmations '(rewrite-front-matter modify-file-name)
00565|   "Make renaming commands prompt for confirmations.
00566| 
00567| This affects the behaviour of renaming commands.  The value is either
00568| nil, in which case no confirmation is ever requested, or a list of
00569| symbols among the following:
00570| 
00571| - `modify-file-name' means that renaming commands will ask for
00572|   confirmation before modifying the file name.
00573| 
00574| - `rewrite-front-matter' means that renaming commands will ask for
00575|   confirmation before rewritting the front matter.
00576| 
00577| - `add-front-matter' means that renaming commands will ask for
00578|   confirmation before adding new front matter to the file.
00579| 
00580| The default behaviour of the `denote-rename-file' command (and others
00581| like it) is to ask for an affirmative answer as a final step before
00582| changing the file name and, where relevant, inserting or updating the
00583| corresponding front matter.
00584| 
00585| Specialized commands that build on top of `denote-rename-file' (or
00586| related) may internally bind this user option to a non-nil value in
00587| order to perform their operation (e.g. `denote-dired-rename-files' goes
00588| through each marked Dired file, prompting for the information to use,
00589| but carries out the renaming without asking for confirmation)."
00590|   :group 'denote
00591|   :type '(radio (const :tag "Disable all confirmations" nil)
00592|                 (set :tag "Available confirmations" :greedy t
00593|                      (const :tag "Add front matter" add-front-matter)
00594|                      (const :tag "Rewrite front matter" rewrite-front-matter)
00595|                      (const :tag "Modify file name" modify-file-name))))

00597| (defcustom denote-excluded-directories-regexp nil
00598|   "Regular expression of directories to exclude from all operations.
00599| Omit matching directories from file prompts and also exclude them
00600| from all functions that check the contents of the variable
00601| `denote-directory'.  The regexp needs to match only the name of
00602| the directory, not its full path.
00603| 
00604| File prompts are used by several commands, such as `denote-link'
00605| and `denote-subdirectory'.
00606| 
00607| Functions that check for files include `denote-directory-files'
00608| and `denote-directory-subdirectories'.
00609| 
00610| The match is performed with `string-match-p'."
00611|   :group 'denote
00612|   :package-version '(denote . "1.2.0")
00613|   :type '(choice (const :tag "Do not filter out anything (default)" nil)
00614|                  (string :tag "Regular expression")))

00667| (defcustom denote-region-after-new-note-functions nil
00668|   "Abnormal hook called after `denote-region'.
00669| Functions in this hook are called with two arguments,
00670| representing the beginning and end buffer positions of the region
00671| that was inserted in the new note.  These are called only if
00672| `denote-region' is invoked while a region is active.
00673| 
00674| A common use-case is to call `org-insert-structure-template'
00675| after a region is inserted.  This case does not actually require
00676| the aforementioned arguments, in which case the function can
00677| simply declare them as ignored by prefixing the argument names
00678| with an underscore.  For example, the following will prompt for a
00679| structure template as soon as `denote-region' is done:
00680| 
00681|     (defun my-denote-region-org-structure-template (_beg _end)
00682|       (when (derived-mode-p \\='org-mode)
00683|         (activate-mark)
00684|         (call-interactively \\='org-insert-structure-template)))
00685| 
00686|     (add-hook \\='denote-region-after-new-note-functions
00687|               #\\='my-denote-region-org-structure-template)"
00688|   :group 'denote
00689|   :package-version '(denote . "2.1.0")
00690|   :link '(info-link "(denote) Create a note with the region's contents")
00691|   :type 'hook)

00693| (defvar denote-prompts-with-history-as-completion
00694|   '(denote-title-prompt denote-signature-prompt denote-files-matching-regexp-prompt denote-query-link-prompt)
00695|   "Prompts that conditionally perform completion against their history.
00696| 
00697| These are minibuffer prompts that ordinarily accept a free form string
00698| input, as opposed to matching against a predefined set.
00699| 
00700| These prompts can optionally perform completion against their own
00701| minibuffer history when the user option `denote-history-completion-in-prompts'
00702| is set to a non-nil value.")
00703| 
00704| (defcustom denote-history-completion-in-prompts t
00705|   "Toggle history completion in all `denote-prompts-with-history-as-completion'.
00706| 
00707| When this user option is set to a non-nil value, use minibuffer history
00708| entries as completion candidates in `denote-prompts-with-history-as-completion'.
00709| Those will show previous inputs from their respective history as
00710| possible values to select, either to (i) re-insert them verbatim or (ii)
00711| with the intent to edit further (depending on the minibuffer user
00712| interface, one can select a candidate with TAB without exiting the
00713| minibuffer, as opposed to what RET normally does by selecting and
00714| exiting).
00715| 
00716| When this user option is set to a nil value, all of the
00717| `denote-prompts-with-history-as-completion' do not use minibuffer
00718| completion: they just prompt for a string of characters.  Their
00719| history is still available through all the standard ways of retrieving
00720| minibuffer history, such as with the command `previous-history-element'.
00721| 
00722| History completion still allows arbitrary values to be provided as
00723| input: they do not have to match the available minibuffer completion
00724| candidates.
00725| 
00726| Note that some prompts, like `denote-keywords-prompt', always use
00727| minibuffer completion, due to the specifics of their data.
00728| 
00729| [ Consider enabling the built-in `savehist-mode' to persist minibuffer
00730|   histories between sessions.]
00731| 
00732| Also see `denote-prompts'."
00733|   :type 'boolean
00734|   :package-version '(denote . "2.3.0")
00735|   :group 'denote)

00752| (defcustom denote-buffer-name-prefix "[D] "
00753|   "String used as the prefix of all buffer names produced by Denote.
00754| This includes the query links, backlinks, `denote-grep', `denote-dired'
00755| buffers, as well as all the regular Denote files whose buffer name gets
00756| updated when `denote-rename-buffer-mode' is enabled (that mode uses the
00757| `denote-rename-buffer-format').
00758| 
00759| By default, the value of `denote-buffer-name-prefix' is \"[D] \".
00760| Users can set it to any string they want, such as \"<Denote> \", or

00766| (defcustom denote-file-name-slug-functions
00767|   '((identifier . identity)
00768|     (title . denote-sluggify-title)
00769|     (signature . denote-sluggify-signature)
00770|     (keyword . denote-sluggify-keyword))
00771|   "Specify the method Denote uses to format the components of the file name.
00772| 
00773| The value is an alist where each element is a cons cell of the
00774| form (COMPONENT . METHOD).
00775| 
00776| - The COMPONENT is an unquoted symbol among `identifier', `title',
00777|   `signature', `keyword' (notice the absence of `s', see below),
00778|   which refers to the corresponding component of the file name.
00779| 
00780| - The METHOD is the function to be used to format the given
00781|   component.  This function should take a string as its parameter
00782|   and return the string formatted for the file name.  In the case
00783|   of the `keyword' component, the function receives a SINGLE
00784|   string representing a single keyword and return it formatted
00785|   for the file name.  Joining the keywords together is handled by
00786|   Denote.
00787| 
00788| Note that the `keyword' function is also applied to the keywords
00789| of the front matter.
00790| 
00791| By default, if a function is not specified for a component, we use
00792| `identity', `denote-sluggify-title', `denote-sluggify-keyword' and
00793| `denote-sluggify-signature'.
00794| 
00795| Remember that deviating from the default file-naming scheme of Denote
00796| will make things harder to search in the future, as files can/will have
00797| permutations that create uncertainty.  The sluggification scheme and
00798| concomitant restrictions we impose by default are there for a very good
00799| reason: they are the distillation of years of experience.  Here we give
00800| you what you wish, but bear in mind it may not be what you need.  You
00801| have been warned."
00802|   :group 'denote
00803|   :package-version '(denote . "2.3.0")
00804|   :link '(info-link "(denote) User-defined sluggification of file name components")
00805|   :type '(alist :key (choice (const title)
00806|                              (const signature)
00807|                              (const keyword))
00808|                 :value function))

00815| (defcustom denote-open-link-function #'find-file-other-window
00816|   "Function to find the file of a Denote link.
00817| 
00818| The default value is `find-file-other-window', with `find-file' because
00819| another common option.  Users can provide a custom function which
00820| behaves like the other two.
00821| 
00822| This is used in all non-Org buffers that have a link created by Denote.
00823| Org has its own mechanism, which you can learn more about by reading the
00824| documentation of the `org-open-at-point' command."
00825|   :group 'denote
00826|   :type '(choice (function :tag "Other window" find-file-other-window)
00827|                  (function :tag "Current window" find-file)
00828|                  (function :tag "Custom function"))

00831| (define-obsolete-variable-alias
00832|   'denote-link-description-function
00833|   'denote-link-description-format
00834|   "4.0.0")
00835| 
00836| (defcustom denote-link-description-format #'denote-link-description-with-signature-and-title
00837|   "The format of a link description text.
00838| This determines how `denote-link' and related functions create a link
00839| description by default.
00840| 
00841| The value can be either a function or a string.  If it is a function, it
00842| is called with two arguments, the file and file type as a symbol among
00843| `denote-file-types'.  It should return a string representing the link
00844| description.  The default is a function that returns the active region
00845| or the title of the note (with the signature if present).
00846| 
00847| For backward compatibility, the function can also take a single
00848| parameter, the given file.  In that case, it is responsible for figuring
00849| out the file type in order to return the correct description.
00850| 
00851| If the value is a string, it treats specially the following specifiers:
00852| 
00853| - The %t is the Denote TITLE in the front matter or the file name.
00854| - The %T is the Denote TITLE in the file name.
00855| - The %i is the Denote IDENTIFIER of the file.
00856| - The %I is the identifier converted to DAYNAME, DAYNUM MONTHNUM YEAR.
00857| - The %d is the same as %i (DATE mnemonic).
00858| - The %D is a \"do what I mean\" which behaves the same as %t and if
00859|   that returns nothing, it falls back to %I, then %i.
00860| - The %s is the Denote SIGNATURE of the file.
00861| - The %k is the Denote KEYWORDS of the file.
00862| - The %% is a literal percent sign.
00863| 
00864| In addition, the following flags are available for each of the specifiers:
00865| 
00866| - 0 :: Pad to the width, if given, with zeros instead of spaces.
00867| - - :: Pad to the width, if given, on the right instead of the left.
00868| - < :: Truncate to the width and precision, if given, on the left.
00869| - > :: Truncate to the width and precision, if given, on the right.
00870| - ^ :: Convert to upper case.
00871| - _ :: Convert to lower case.
00872| 
00873| When combined all together, the above are written thus:
00874| 
00875|     %<flags><width><precision>SPECIFIER-CHARACTER
00876| 
00877| Any other text in the string it taken as-is.  Users may want, for
00878| example, to include some text that makes Denote links stand out, such as
00879| a [D] prefix.
00880| 
00881| If the region is active, its text is used as the link's description."
00882|   :type '(choice
00883|           (string :tag "String with treats format specifiers specially")
00884|           (function :tag "Custom function like `denote-link-description-with-signature-and-title'"))
00885|   :package-version '(denote . "4.0.0")
00886|   :group 'denote)

00926| ;;;; File helper functions

00928| (defun denote-get-completion-table (candidates &rest metadata)
00929|   "Return completion table with CANDIDATES and METADATA.
00930| CANDIDATES is a list of strings.  METADATA is described in
00931| `completion-metadata'."
00932|   (lambda (string pred action)
00933|     (if (eq action 'metadata)
00934|         (cons 'metadata metadata)
00935|       (complete-with-action action candidates string pred))))
00936| 
00937| (defun denote--default-directory-is-silo-p ()
00938|   "Return path to silo if `default-directory' is a silo."
00939|   (when-let* ((dir-locals (dir-locals-find-file default-directory))
00940|               ((alist-get 'denote-directory dir-local-variables-alist)))
00941|     (cond
00942|      ((listp dir-locals)
00943|       (car dir-locals))
00944|      ((stringp dir-locals)
00945|       dir-locals))))
00946| 
00947| (defun denote-directories--make-paths (directories)
00948|   "Call `make-directory' on each element of DIRECTORIES unless it exists.
00949| Make any parent directories as well."
00950|   (dolist (directory directories)
00951|     (unless (file-directory-p directory)
00952|       (make-directory directory :parents))))
00953| 
00954| (defun denote-directories--get-paths ()
00955|   "Return variable `denote-directory' as a list of directory paths."
00956|   (let ((get-dir (lambda (directory) (file-name-as-directory (expand-file-name directory)))))
00957|     (if (listp denote-directory)
00958|         (mapcar get-dir denote-directory)
00959|       (list (funcall get-dir denote-directory)))))
00960| 
00961| (defun denote-directories ()
00962|   "Return path of variable `denote-directory' as a proper directory.
00963| If the variable `denote-directory' is set to a list of file paths,
00964| return the list with each element expanded to be a directory.  Create
00965| any directories and their parents, if needed.
00966| 
00967| Custom Lisp code can `let' bind the variable `denote-directory'
00968| to override what this function returns."
00969|   (if-let* (((or (eq denote-directory 'default-directory) (eq denote-directory 'local)))
00970|             (silo-dir (denote--default-directory-is-silo-p)))
00971|       (progn
00972|         (display-warning
00973|          'denote
00974|          "Silo value must be a string; `local' or `default-directory' are obsolete"
00975|          :error)
00976|         (list silo-dir))
00977|     (let ((denote-directories (denote-directories--get-paths)))
00978|       (denote-directories--make-paths denote-directories)
00979|       denote-directories)))
00980| 
00981| (defun denote-has-single-denote-directory-p ()
00982|   "Return non-nil if the variable `denote-directory' is a single item."
00983|   (not (cdr (denote-directories))))
00984| 
00985| (defun denote--get-common-root-directory (directories)
00986|   "Return common root directory among DIRECTORIES."
00987|   (if-let* ((parts (mapcar (lambda (directory) (split-string directory "/" :omit-nulls)) directories))
00988|             (common-parent (seq-reduce
00989|                             (lambda (dir-parts comparison-parts)
00990|                               (let ((common nil))
00991|                                 (dolist (part dir-parts)
00992|                                   (when (member part comparison-parts)
00993|                                     (push part common)))
00994|                                 (nreverse common)))
00995|                             parts (car parts))))
00996|       (format "/%s/" (mapconcat #'identity common-parent "/"))
00997|     "/"))
00998| 
00999| (defun denote-directories-get-common-root ()
01000|   "Get the common root directory of `denote-directories'."
01001|   (denote--get-common-root-directory (denote-directories)))
01002| 
01003| (defun denote-directory ()
01004|   "Return the `car' of `denote-directories'.
01005| Unless this is definitely what you need, use the `denote-directories'
01006| instead.  Also see `denote-directories-get-common-root'."
01007|   (car (denote-directories)))

01011| (defvar denote-generate-identifier-automatically t
01012|   "Make creation and renaming commands automatically create and identifier.
01013| 
01014| This applies when a note is created or renamed.  The default is to
01015| always create an identifier automatically.
01016| 
01017| Valid values are: t, nil, `on-creation', and `on-rename'.")

01022| ;;;;; Sluggification functions
01023| 
01024| (defun denote-slug-keep-only-ascii (str)
01025|   "Remove all non-ASCII characters from STR and replace them with spaces.
01026| This is useful as a helper function to construct
01027| `denote-file-name-slug-functions'."
01028|   (let* ((ascii-range (seq-map
01029|                        (lambda (character)
01030|                          (if (and (>= character 33) (<= character 126))
01031|                              character
01032|                            32)) ; empty space
01033|                        str))
01034|          (characters (seq-filter #'characterp ascii-range)))
01035|     (mapconcat #'string characters)))
01036| 
01037| (define-obsolete-function-alias
01038|   'denote--slug-hyphenate
01039|   'denote-slug-hyphenate
01040|   "4.0.0")
01041| 
01042| (defun denote-slug-hyphenate (str)
01043|   "Replace spaces and underscores with hyphens in STR.
01044| Also replace multiple hyphens with a single one and remove any
01045| leading and trailing hyphen."
01046|   (replace-regexp-in-string
01047|    "^-\\|-$" ""
01048|    (replace-regexp-in-string
01049|     "-\\{2,\\}" "-"
01050|     (replace-regexp-in-string "_\\|\s+" "-" str))))
01051| 
01052| (defun denote-slug-put-equals (str)
01053|   "Replace spaces and underscores with equals signs in STR.
01054| Also replace multiple equals signs with a single one and remove
01055| any leading and trailing signs."
01056|   (replace-regexp-in-string
01057|    "^=\\|=$" ""
01058|    (replace-regexp-in-string
01059|     "=\\{2,\\}" "="
01060|     (replace-regexp-in-string "_\\|\s+" "=" str))))
01061| 
01062| (defun denote--valid-identifier (identifier)
01063|   "Ensure that IDENTIFIER is valid.
01064| 
01065| It must not contain square brackets, parenthesis, \"query-filenames:\"
01066| or \"query-contents\"."
01067|   (replace-regexp-in-string
01068|    "query-filenames:" ""
01069|    (replace-regexp-in-string
01070|     "query-contents:" ""
01071|     (replace-regexp-in-string
01072|      "[][()]*" "" identifier))))
01073| 
01074| (defun denote--remove-dot-characters (str)
01075|   "Remove dot characters from STR."
01076|   (replace-regexp-in-string "\\." "" str))
01077| 
01078| (defun denote--trim-right-token-characters (str component)
01079|   "Remove =, -, _ and @ from the end of STR.
01080| The removal is done only if necessary according to COMPONENT."
01081|   (if (eq component 'title)
01082|       (string-trim-right str "[=@_]+")
01083|     (string-trim-right str "[=@_-]+")))
01084| 
01085| (defun denote--replace-consecutive-token-characters (str component)
01086|   "Replace consecutive characters with a single one in STR.
01087| Hyphens, underscores, equal signs and at signs are replaced with
01088| a single one in str, if necessary according to COMPONENT."
01089|   (let ((str (replace-regexp-in-string
01090|               "_\\{2,\\}" "_"
01091|               (replace-regexp-in-string
01092|                "=\\{2,\\}" "="
01093|                (replace-regexp-in-string
01094|                 "@\\{2,\\}" "@" str)))))
01095|     ;; -- are allowed in titles when the default sluggification is disabled
01096|     (if (eq component 'title)
01097|         str
01098|       (replace-regexp-in-string
01099|        "-\\{2,\\}" "-" str))))
01100| 
01101| (defun denote-sluggify-and-apply-rules (component str)
01102|   "Make STR an appropriate slug for file name COMPONENT.
01103| 
01104| Apply the function specified in `denote-file-name-slug-function' to
01105| COMPONENT which is one of `identifier', `title', `signature', `keyword'.
01106| If the resulting string still contains consecutive -, _, =, or @, they
01107| are replaced by a single occurence of the character, if necessary
01108| according to COMPONENT.  If COMPONENT is `keyword', remove underscores
01109| from STR as they are used as the keywords separator in file names.
01110| 
01111| Also enforce the rules of the file-naming scheme."
01112|   (let* ((slug-function (alist-get component denote-file-name-slug-functions))
01113|          (str-slug (pcase component
01114|                      ('title (funcall (or slug-function #'denote-sluggify-title) str))
01115|                      ('keyword (replace-regexp-in-string
01116|                                 "_" ""
01117|                                 (funcall (or slug-function #'denote-sluggify-keyword) str)))
01118|                      ('identifier (denote--valid-identifier (funcall (or slug-function #'identity) str)))
01119|                      ('signature (funcall (or slug-function #'denote-sluggify-signature) str)))))
01120|     (thread-first
01121|       (denote--remove-dot-characters str-slug)
01122|       (denote--replace-consecutive-token-characters component)
01123|       (denote--trim-right-token-characters component))))
01124| 
01125| (defalias 'denote-sluggify 'denote-sluggify-and-apply-rules
01126|   "Alias for the function `denote-sluggify-and-apply-rules'.")
01127| 
01128| (defun denote-sluggify-title (str)
01129|   "Make STR an appropriate slug for title."
01130|   (downcase
01131|    (denote-slug-hyphenate
01132|     (replace-regexp-in-string "[][{}!@#$%^&*()+'\"?,.\|;:~`‘’“”/=]*" "" str))))
01133| 
01134| (defun denote-sluggify-signature (str)
01135|   "Make STR an appropriate slug for signature."
01136|   (downcase
01137|    (denote-slug-put-equals
01138|     (replace-regexp-in-string "[][{}!@#$%^&*()+'\"?,.\|;:~`‘’“”/-]*" "" str))))
01139| 
01140| (defun denote-sluggify-keyword (str)
01141|   "Sluggify STR while joining separate words."
01142|   (downcase
01143|    (replace-regexp-in-string "[][{}!@#$%^&*()+'\"?,.\|;:~`‘’“”/_ =-]*" "" str)))
01144| 
01145| (defun denote-sluggify-keywords-and-apply-rules (keywords)
01146|   "Sluggify KEYWORDS, which is a list of strings."
01147|   (mapcar (lambda (keyword)
01148|             (denote-sluggify-and-apply-rules 'keyword keyword))
01149|           keywords))
01150| 
01151| (defalias 'denote-sluggify-keywords 'denote-sluggify-keywords-and-apply-rules
01152|   "Alias for the function `denote-sluggify-keywords-and-apply-rules'.")
01153|

01198|   "Return non-nil if FILE is an actual Denote note.
01199| For our purposes, a note must satisfy `file-regular-p' and
01200| `denote-filename-is-note-p'."

01203| (define-obsolete-function-alias
01204|   'denote-filename-is-note-p
01205|   'denote-file-has-denoted-filename-p
01206|   "4.1.0")
01207| 
01208| (define-obsolete-function-alias
01209|   'denote-file-is-note-p
01210|   'denote-file-has-denoted-filename-p
01211|   "4.1.0")
01212| 
01213| (defun denote-file-has-denoted-filename-p (file)
01214|   "Return non-nil if FILE respects the file-naming scheme of Denote.
01215| 
01216| This tests the rules of Denote's file-naming scheme.  Sluggification is
01217| ignored.  It is done by removing all file name components and validating
01218| what remains."
01219|   (let* ((initial-filename (file-name-nondirectory file))
01220|          (filename initial-filename)
01221|          (title (denote-retrieve-filename-title file))
01222|          (keywords-string (denote-retrieve-filename-keywords file))
01223|          (signature (denote-retrieve-filename-signature file))
01224|          (identifier (denote-retrieve-filename-identifier file)))
01225|     (when title
01226|       (setq filename (replace-regexp-in-string (concat "\\(--" (regexp-quote title) "\\).*\\'") "" filename nil nil 1)))
01227|     (when keywords-string
01228|       (setq filename (replace-regexp-in-string (concat "\\(__" (regexp-quote keywords-string) "\\).*\\'") "" filename nil nil 1)))
01229|     (when signature
01230|       (setq filename (replace-regexp-in-string (concat "\\(==" (regexp-quote signature) "\\).*\\'") "" filename nil nil 1)))
01231|     (when identifier
01232|       (if (string-match-p "@@" filename)
01233|           (setq filename (replace-regexp-in-string (concat "\\(@@" (regexp-quote identifier) "\\).*\\'") "" filename nil nil 1))
01234|         (setq filename (replace-regexp-in-string (concat "\\(" (regexp-quote identifier) "\\).*\\'") "" filename nil nil 1))))
01235|     ;; What remains should be the empty string or the file extension.
01236|     (and (not (string-prefix-p "." initial-filename))
01237|          (or (string-empty-p filename)
01238|              (string-prefix-p "." filename)))))
01239| 
01240| (defun denote-file-has-signature-p (file)
01241|   "Return non-nil if FILE has a Denote identifier."
01242|   (denote-retrieve-filename-signature file))
01243| 
01244| (defun denote-file-is-writable-and-supported-p (file)
01245|   "Return non-nil if FILE is writable and has supported extension."
01246|   ;; We do not want to test that the file is regular (exists) because we want
01247|   ;; this function to return t on files that are still unsaved.
01248|   (and (file-writable-p file)
01249|        (denote-file-has-supported-extension-p file)))
01250| 
01251| (defun denote--get-file-name-relative-to-directories (file directories)
01252|   "Return FILE relative to one of the DIRECTORIES."
01253|   (unless (file-name-absolute-p file)
01254|     (error "The file `%s' is not absolute" file))
01255|   (when-let* ((directory (seq-find
01256|                           (lambda (d)
01257|                             (string-prefix-p d file))
01258|                           directories)))
01259|     (substring-no-properties file (length directory))))

01270| (defun denote--exclude-directory-regexp-p (file)
01271|   "Return non-nil if FILE matches `denote-excluded-directories-regexp'."
01272|   (and (stringp denote-excluded-directories-regexp)
01273|        (string-match-p denote-excluded-directories-regexp file)))

01275| (defun denote--directory-all-files-recursively ()
01276|   "Return list of all files in variable `denote-directories'.
01277| Avoids traversing dotfiles (unconditionally) and whatever matches
01278| `denote-excluded-directories-regexp'."
01279|   (let* ((directories (denote-directories))
01280|          (predicate-fn
01281|           (lambda (file)
01282|             (let ((rel (denote--get-file-name-relative-to-directories file directories)))
01283|               (cond
01284|                ((string-match-p "\\`\\." rel) nil)
01285|                ((string-match-p "/\\." rel) nil)
01286|                ((denote--exclude-directory-regexp-p rel) nil)
01287|                ((file-readable-p file)))))))
01288|     (apply #'append
01289|            (mapcar
01290|             (lambda (directory)
01291|               (directory-files-recursively
01292|                directory
01293|                directory-files-no-dot-files-regexp
01294|                :include-directories
01295|                predicate-fn
01296|                :follow-symlinks))
01297|             directories))))
01298| 
01299| (defun denote--file-excluded-p (file)
01300|   "Return non-file if FILE matches `denote-excluded-files-regexp'."
01301|   (and denote-excluded-files-regexp
01302|        (string-match-p denote-excluded-files-regexp file)))
01303| 
01304| (defun denote--directory-get-files ()
01305|   "Return list with full path of valid files in variable `denote-directory'.
01306| Consider files that satisfy `denote-file-has-denoted-filename-p' and
01307| are not backups."
01308|   (seq-filter
01309|    (lambda (file)
01310|      (and (file-regular-p file)
01311|           (denote-file-has-denoted-filename-p file)
01312|           (not (denote--file-excluded-p file))
01313|           (not (backup-file-name-p file))))
01314|    (denote--directory-all-files-recursively)))
01315| 
01316| (make-obsolete-variable
01317|  'denote-directory-get-files-function
01318|  "advanced users should write an advice for `denote-directory-files'"
01319|  "4.2.0")
01320| 
01321| ;; The HAS-IDENTIFIER is there because we support cases where files do
01322| ;; not have an identifier.
01323| (defun denote-directory-files (&optional files-matching-regexp omit-current text-only exclude-regexp has-identifier)
01324|   "Return list of absolute file paths in variable `denote-directory'.
01325| Files that match `denote-excluded-files-regexp' are excluded from the
01326| list.
01327| 
01328| Files only need to have an identifier.  The return value may thus
01329| include file types that are not implied by the variable
01330| `denote-file-type'.
01331| 
01332| With optional FILES-MATCHING-REGEXP, restrict files to those
01333| matching the given regular expression.
01334| 
01335| With optional OMIT-CURRENT as a non-nil value, do not include the
01336| current Denote file in the returned list.
01337| 
01338| With optional TEXT-ONLY as a non-nil value, limit the results to
01339| text files that satisfy `denote-file-has-supported-extension-p'.
01340| 
01341| With optional EXCLUDE-REGEXP exclude the files that match the given
01342| regular expression.  This is done after FILES-MATCHING-REGEXP and
01343| OMIT-CURRENT have been applied.
01344| 
01345| With optional HAS-IDENTIFIER as a non-nil value, limit the results to
01346| files that have an identifier."
01347|   (let ((files (denote--directory-get-files)))
01348|     (when (and omit-current buffer-file-name (denote-file-has-identifier-p buffer-file-name))
01349|       (setq files (delete buffer-file-name files)))
01350|     (when files-matching-regexp
01351|       (let ((dirs (denote-directories)))
01352|         (setq files (seq-filter
01353|                      (lambda (f)
01354|                        (string-match-p files-matching-regexp (denote--get-file-name-relative-to-directories f dirs)))
01355|                      files))))
01356|     (when text-only
01357|       (setq files (seq-filter #'denote-file-has-supported-extension-p files)))
01358|     (when has-identifier
01359|       (setq files (seq-filter #'denote-file-has-identifier-p files)))
01360|     (when exclude-regexp
01361|       (setq files (seq-remove
01362|                    (lambda (file)
01363|                      (string-match-p exclude-regexp file))
01364|                    files)))
01365|     files))
01366| 
01367| (defun denote-directory-subdirectories ()
01368|   "Return list of subdirectories in variable `denote-directory'.
01369| Omit dotfiles (such as .git) unconditionally.  Also exclude
01370| whatever matches `denote-excluded-directories-regexp'."
01371|   (let ((dirs (denote-directories)))
01372|     (seq-remove
01373|      (lambda (filename)
01374|        (let ((rel (denote--get-file-name-relative-to-directories filename dirs)))
01375|          (or (not (file-directory-p filename))
01376|              (string-match-p "\\`\\." rel)
01377|              (string-match-p "/\\." rel)
01378|              (denote--exclude-directory-regexp-p rel))))
01379|      (denote--directory-all-files-recursively))))
01380| 
01381| ;; TODO 2023-01-24: Perhaps there is a good reason to make this a user
01382| ;; option, but I am keeping it as a generic variable for now.
01383| (defvar denote-encryption-file-extensions '(".gpg" ".age")
01384|   "List of strings specifying file extensions for encryption.")
01385| 
01386| (defun denote-file-type-extensions-with-encryption ()
01387|   "Derive `denote-file-type-extensions' plus `denote-encryption-file-extensions'."
01388|   (let ((file-extensions (denote-file-type-extensions))
01389|         all)
01390|     (dolist (ext file-extensions)
01391|       (dolist (enc denote-encryption-file-extensions)
01392|         (push (concat ext enc) all)))
01393|     (append file-extensions all)))
01394| 
01395| (defun denote-get-file-extension (file)
01396|   "Return extension of FILE with dot included.
01397| Account for `denote-encryption-file-extensions'.  In other words,
01398| return something like .org.gpg if it is part of the file, else
01399| return .org."
01400|   (let ((outer-extension (file-name-extension file :period)))
01401|     (if-let* (((member outer-extension denote-encryption-file-extensions))
01402|               (file (file-name-sans-extension file))
01403|               (inner-extension (file-name-extension file :period)))
01404|         (concat inner-extension outer-extension)
01405|       outer-extension)))
01406| 
01407| (defun denote-get-file-extension-sans-encryption (file)
01408|   "Return extension of FILE with dot included and without the encryption part.
01409| Build on top of `denote-get-file-extension' though always return
01410| something like .org even if the actual file extension is
01411| .org.gpg."
01412|   (let ((extension (denote-get-file-extension file)))
01413|     (if (string-match (regexp-opt denote-encryption-file-extensions) extension)
01414|         (substring extension 0 (match-beginning 0))
01415|       extension)))
01416| 
01417| (defun denote-get-path-by-id (id)
01418|   "Return absolute path of ID string in `denote-directory-files'."
01419|   (let ((files
01420|          (seq-filter
01421|           (lambda (file)
01422|             (string= id (denote-retrieve-filename-identifier file)))
01423|           (denote-directory-files nil nil nil nil :has-identifier))))
01424|     (if (length< files 2)
01425|         (car files)
01426|       (seq-find
01427|        (lambda (file)
01428|          (let ((file-extension (denote-get-file-extension-sans-encryption file)))
01429|            (and (denote-file-has-supported-extension-p file)
01430|                 (or (string= (denote--file-extension denote-file-type)
01431|                              file-extension)
01432|                     (string= ".org" file-extension)
01433|                     (member file-extension (denote-file-type-extensions))))))
01434|        files))))
01435| 
01436| (defun denote-get-relative-path-by-id (id &optional directory)
01437|   "Return relative path of ID string in `denote-directory-files'.
01438| The path is relative to DIRECTORY (default: ‘default-directory’)."
01439|   (when-let* ((path (denote-get-path-by-id id)))
01440|     (file-relative-name path directory)))

01453| (defvar denote-file-prompt-use-files-matching-regexp nil

01456| there.")

01458| (defun denote-file-prompt-group (file transform)
01459|   "Retun group of FILE if TRANSFORM is non-nil, per `completion-metadata'."
01460|   (cond
01461|    ;; FIXME 2025-12-16: Why do we not get highlights of matched
01462|    ;; visible words?  It works if I just return FILE.
01463|    (transform (or (denote-retrieve-filename-title file) file))
01464|    ((file-name-directory file))
01465|    ((file-name-extension file))
01466|    (t "Other files")))
01467| 
01468| (defun denote-file-prompt--format-identifier (file)
01469|   "Return identifier of FILE for `denote-file-prompt-affixate'."
01470|   (let* ((identifier (denote-retrieve-filename-identifier file))
01471|          (date-or-id (or (ignore-errors (denote-id-to-date identifier)) identifier))
01472|          (propertized (propertize date-or-id 'face 'completions-annotations)))
01473|     (format "%s " propertized)))
01474| 
01475| (defun denote-file-prompt--format-keywords-and-signature (file)
01476|   "Return keywords and signature of FILE for `denote-file-prompt-affixate'."
01477|   (let ((keywords (denote-retrieve-filename-keywords file))
01478|         (signature (denote-retrieve-filename-signature file)))
01479|     (when-let* ((combined (cond
01480|                            ((and keywords signature) (concat "=" signature "  " keywords))
01481|                            (keywords)
01482|                            (signature))))
01483|       (format " %s%s"
01484|               (if (eq completions-format 'one-column)
01485|                   (propertize " " 'display '(space :align-to 90))
01486|                 " ")
01487|               (propertize combined 'face 'completions-annotations)))))
01488| 
01489| (defun denote-file-prompt-affixate (files)
01490|   "Affixate FILES.
01491| Use the identifier as a prefix and the keywords as a suffix."
01492|   (mapcar
01493|    (lambda (file)
01494|      (list
01495|       file
01496|       (or (denote-file-prompt--format-identifier file) "")
01497|       (or (denote-file-prompt--format-keywords-and-signature file) "")))
01498|    files))
01499| 
01500| (defun denote-file-prompt-sort (files)
01501|   "Sort FILES for `denote-file-prompt', per `completion-metadata'."
01502|   (sort files #'denote-sort-modified-time-greaterp))
01503| 
01504| (defvar denote-file-prompt-extra-metadata
01505|   (list
01506|    ;; NOTE 2025-12-15: If we use the `file' category, then we are
01507|    ;; subject to the `completion-category-overrides'.  This is a
01508|    ;; problem because the user will want to, for example, sort
01509|    ;; directories before files, but then we cannot have our sort here.
01510|    (cons 'category 'denote-file)
01511|    (cons 'group-function #'denote-file-prompt-group)
01512|    (cons 'affixation-function #'denote-file-prompt-affixate)
01513|    (cons 'display-sort-function #'denote-file-prompt-sort))
01514|   "Extra `completion-metadata' for the `denote-file-prompt'.
01515| This is in addition to the completion category, which is constant.")
01516| 
01517| (with-eval-after-load 'all-the-icons
01518|   (cl-defmethod all-the-icons-completion-get-icon (cand (_cat (eql denote-file)))
01519|     "Return the icon for the candidate CAND of completion category denote-file."
01520|     (all-the-icons-completion-get-icon cand 'file)))
01521| 
01522| (with-eval-after-load 'nerd-icons
01523|   (cl-defmethod nerd-icons-completion-get-icon (cand (_cat (eql denote-file)))
01524|     "Return the icon for the candidate CAND of completion category denote-file."
01525|     (nerd-icons-completion-get-icon cand 'file)))
01526| 
01527| (defun denote-file-prompt (&optional files-matching-regexp prompt-text no-require-match has-identifier)
01528|   "Prompt for file in variable `denote-directory'.
01529| Files that match `denote-excluded-files-regexp' are excluded from the
01530| list.
01531| 
01532| With optional FILES-MATCHING-REGEXP, filter the candidates per
01533| the given regular expression.
01534| 
01535| With optional PROMPT-TEXT, use it instead of the default call to
01536| select a file.
01537| 
01538| With optional NO-REQUIRE-MATCH, accept the given input as-is.
01539| 
01540| With optional HAS-IDENTIFIER, only show candidates that have an
01541| identifier.
01542| 
01543| Return the absolute path to the matching file."
01544|   (let* ((roots (denote-directories))
01545|          (single-dir-p (null (cdr roots)))
01546|          ;; Some external program may use `default-directory' with the
01547|          ;; relative file paths of the completion candidates.
01548|          (default-directory (if single-dir-p
01549|                                 (car roots)
01550|                               (denote-directories-get-common-root)))
01551|          (files (denote-directory-files
01552|                  (or denote-file-prompt-use-files-matching-regexp files-matching-regexp)
01553|                  :omit-current nil nil has-identifier))
01554|          (relative-files (if single-dir-p
01555|                              (mapcar
01556|                               (lambda (file)
01557|                                 (denote--get-file-name-relative-to-directories file roots))
01558|                               files)
01559|                            files))
01560|          (prompt (if single-dir-p
01561|                      (format "%s: " (or prompt-text "Select FILE"))
01562|                    (format "%s in %s: "
01563|                            (or prompt-text "Select FILE")
01564|                            (propertize default-directory 'face 'denote-faces-prompt-current-name))))
01565|          (input (completing-read
01566|                  prompt
01567|                  (apply 'denote-get-completion-table relative-files denote-file-prompt-extra-metadata)
01568|                  nil (unless no-require-match t)
01569|                  nil 'denote-file-history))
01570|          (absolute-file (if single-dir-p
01571|                             (expand-file-name input default-directory)
01572|                           input)))
01573|     ;; NOTE: This block is executed when no-require-match is t. It is useful
01574|     ;; for commands such as `denote-open-or-create' or similar.
01575|     (unless (file-exists-p absolute-file)
01576|       (setq denote-file-prompt-latest-input input)
01577|       (setq denote-file-history (delete input denote-file-history)))
01578|     ;; NOTE: We must always return an absolute path, even if it does not
01579|     ;; exist, because callers expect one.  They handle a non-existent file
01580|     ;; appropriately.
01581|     absolute-file))
01582| 
01583| (defun denote-format-buffer-name (string &optional special)
01584|   "Use STRING to return a Denote buffer name with `denote-buffer-name-prefix'.
01585| With optional SPECIAL, wrap the name in asterisks, signifying that this
01586| is a special buffer."
01587|   (format (if special "*%s%s*" "%s%s") denote-buffer-name-prefix string))
01588| 
01589| ;;;; The sort mechanism
```
